        <td id="L195" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="195"></td>
        <td id="LC195" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>\address[mymainaddress]{1600 John F Kennedy Boulevard, Philadelphia}</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L196" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="196"></td>
        <td id="LC196" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>\address[mysecondaryaddress]{360 Park Avenue South, New York}</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L197" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="197"></td>
        <td id="LC197" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L198" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="198"></td>
        <td id="LC198" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{<span class="pl-smi">abstract</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L199" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="199"></td>
        <td id="LC199" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We have demonstrated in previous work that the Calculus of Covalent Bonding (CCB) can be used to simulate higher-level biochemical processes. This is significant since CCB was originally devised to model organic chemical reactions on a lower level. We are now extending the use of CCB to model another gene repair pathway, DNA Mismatch Repair (MMR). This is a more complex pathway than the Base Excision Repair (BER) which we modelled originally. It involves four proteins and needs a distinction between the two chains in a DNA strand. We demonstrate that we can model this by extending our modelling of BER and that we can do this using the unchanged CCB calculus and operational semantics. We also show that the simulation software developed previously can be used to execute this pathway.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L200" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="200"></td>
        <td id="LC200" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{<span class="pl-smi">abstract</span>}</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC211" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{<span class="pl-en">Introduction</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L212" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="212"></td>
        <td id="LC212" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Probably write this last, once we have the rest</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L213" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="213"></td>

</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L214" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="214"></td>
        <td id="LC214" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{<span class="pl-en">A Calculus of Covalent Bonding</span>}<span class="pl-k">\label</span>{<span class="pl-v">sec:calculus</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L215" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="215"></td>
        <td id="LC215" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L216" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="216"></td>
        <td id="LC216" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This is from socp paper, needs reworking</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L217" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="217"></td>
        <td id="LC217" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L218" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="218"></td>
        <td id="LC218" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In this section we define the calculus introduced informally in the Introduction. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L219" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="219"></td>
        <td id="LC219" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">First, we introduce some preliminary notions and notations.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L220" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="220"></td>
        <td id="LC220" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L221" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="221"></td>
        <td id="LC221" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mA</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be the set of (forward) action labels, </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L222" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="222"></td>
        <td id="LC222" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">ranged over by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a,b,c,d,e,f<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. We partition <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mA</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> into the set of <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-mi">strong actions</span>}, written as</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L223" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="223"></td>
        <td id="LC223" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mSA</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and the set of <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-mi">weak actions</span>}, written as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mWA</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. Reverse (or past) action labels are members of</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L224" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="224"></td>
        <td id="LC224" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\underline\mA</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, with typical members <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\un</span>{a},<span class="pl-c1">\un</span> b, <span class="pl-c1">\un</span> c,<span class="pl-c1">\un</span> d, <span class="pl-c1">\un</span> e ,<span class="pl-c1">\un</span> f<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and represent </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L225" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="225"></td>
        <td id="LC225" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">undoing of actions. The set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathcal</span>{P}(<span class="pl-c1">\mA</span> <span class="pl-c1">\cup</span> <span class="pl-c1">\underline\mA</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is ranged over by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L226" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="226"></td>
        <td id="LC226" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L227" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="227"></td>
        <td id="LC227" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Keys</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be an infinite set of {<span class="pl-c1">\em</span> communication keys} (or {<span class="pl-c1">\em</span> keys} for short)</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L228" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="228"></td>
        <td id="LC228" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-k">\cite</span>{<span class="pl-c1">PhillipsUlidowski06</span>,<span class="pl-c1">Irek2007</span>}, ranged over by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>k,l, m,n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. The Cartesian product <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathcal</span> A <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Keys</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, denoted by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mAK</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L229" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="229"></td>
        <td id="LC229" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> represents past actions, which are written as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a[k]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a<span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mA</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>k<span class="pl-c1">\in</span><span class="pl-c1">\Keys</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L230" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="230"></td>
        <td id="LC230" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Correspondingly, we have the set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\umAK</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> that represents undoing of past actions. We use <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\beta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to identify actions which are either from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mA</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> or <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mAK</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. It would be </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L231" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="231"></td>
        <td id="LC231" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">useful to consider sequences of actions or past actions, namely the elements of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mA</span> <span class="pl-c1">\cup</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mAK</span>)^*<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L232" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="232"></td>
        <td id="LC232" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">which are ranged over by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s,s&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and sequences of purely past actions, namely the elements of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mAK</span>^*<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L233" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="233"></td>
        <td id="LC233" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">which are ranged over by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t,t&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. The empty sequence is denoted by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\epsilon</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. We use the notation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>, s<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L234" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="234"></td>
        <td id="LC234" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s,s&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to denote a concatenation of elements, which can be strings or single actions.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L235" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="235"></td>
        <td id="LC235" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L236" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="236"></td>
        <td id="LC236" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We shall also use two sets of auxiliary action labels, namely the set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mA</span>) =<span class="pl-cce">\{</span> (a)<span class="pl-cce">\ </span><span class="pl-c1">\mid</span> a<span class="pl-c1">\in</span><span class="pl-c1">\mA</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and its product with the set of keys, namely <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mA</span>)<span class="pl-c1">\Keys</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. These labels will be used in the auxiliary rules when defining</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L237" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="237"></td>
        <td id="LC237" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">the semantics of CCB.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L238" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="238"></td>
        <td id="LC238" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L239" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="239"></td>
        <td id="LC239" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We now define the Calculus of Covalent Bonding, or CCB for short. The syntax of CCB is given </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L240" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="240"></td>

        <td id="LC300" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A context <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-c1">\hole</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a process term containing a <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-mi">hole</span>}, represented by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\hole</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L301" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="301"></td>
        <td id="LC301" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Formally, contexts are defined by</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L302" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="302"></td>
        <td id="LC302" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">the following syntax: <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C::= <span class="pl-c1">\hole</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mid</span> (s;b).C <span class="pl-c1">\mid</span> P<span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> C <span class="pl-c1">\mid</span> C <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> P <span class="pl-c1">\mid</span> C<span class="pl-c1">\restrict</span> L <span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L303" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="303"></td>
        <td id="LC303" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The term <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C[Q]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> denotes the result of filling the hole in the context <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-c1">\hole</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the process <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L304" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="304"></td>
        <td id="LC304" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We say that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-mi">subprocess</span>} of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> if <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C[R]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for some context <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-c1">\hole</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>

</td>

        <td id="LC306" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We define the semantics of our calculus by a labelled transition system,</td>

        <td id="LC457" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">process <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(a;b).(c) <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> (a,d,c)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and the communication function <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> given by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(a,a)=a<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> </td>

      </tr>

This is because <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(c)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> </td>

        <td id="L613" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="613"></td>
        <td id="LC613" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The next example illustrates how some of the reverse SOS rules work.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L614" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="614"></td>
        <td id="LC614" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{<span class="pl-smi">example</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L615" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="615"></td>
        <td id="LC615" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">{<span class="pl-c1">\rm</span> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L616" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="616"></td>
        <td id="LC616" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Consider <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(a[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>],b).(c).S<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S<span class="pl-c1">\bydef</span> (a,b).(c).S<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. We have </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L617" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="617"></td>
        <td id="LC617" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span>(a[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>],b).(c).S <span class="pl-c1">\xrightarrow</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\underline</span>{a}[1]} (a,b).(c).S<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span> by <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{rev act1} since <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(c).S<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is standard.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L618" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="618"></td>
        <td id="LC618" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Since <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(a,b).(c).S<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the definition of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we obtain by rule <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{rev con} <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(a[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>],b).(c).S <span class="pl-c1">\xrightarrow</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\underline</span>{a}[1]} S<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L619" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="619"></td>
        <td id="LC619" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">}</td>
      </tr>

</td>

        <td id="L622" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="622"></td>
        <td id="LC622" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Figure <span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">fig:csos</span>} contains the SOS rules that define the new concerted actions transitions. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L623" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="623"></td>
        <td id="LC623" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The main rule is the rule <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{concert} that defines when a pair of concerted actions </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L624" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="624"></td>
        <td id="LC624" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">takes place.  We also have two auxiliary rules <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{aux1} and <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{aux2} which </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L625" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="625"></td>
        <td id="LC625" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">define only an auxiliary transition relation needed in the <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{concert} rule. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L626" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="626"></td>
        <td id="LC626" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Note that the <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{concert} rule uses <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-mi">lookahead</span>} <span class="pl-k">\cite</span>{<span class="pl-c1">Uli92</span>}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L627" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="627"></td>
        <td id="LC627" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Also note that transitions in <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{aux1} and <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{aux2} use the auxiliary labels <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(b)[k]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L628" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="628"></td>
        <td id="LC628" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">for all <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mWA</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>k <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Keys</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. The rule <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{concert par} requires that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is fresh in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L629" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="629"></td>
        <td id="LC629" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">correspondingly as in <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{par}. Moreover, we need to ensure that when we reverse <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>h<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the key <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>l<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span></td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L630" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="630"></td>
        <td id="LC630" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we do not leave out any actions with the key <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>l<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> which make up a multiaction </td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC631" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">communication with the key <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>l<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. Hence, we also include the premise <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\fresh</span>{l}{Q}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{concert par}.</td>
      </tr>

      </tr>

        <td id="L633" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="633"></td>
        <td id="LC633" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Our operational semantics guarantees that if a standard process evolves to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(t;b).P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, for some <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and</td>
      </tr>

First we define the function <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{fn}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for {<span class="pl-c1">\em</span> free names} of processes.</td>

        <td id="L684" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="684"></td>

        <td id="LC786" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">part tells us how to use the remaining rules to define transitions. If <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has no <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{prom}, </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L787" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="787"></td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L788" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="788"></td>
        <td id="LC788" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">required to reduce <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{prom}, <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{move-r} and <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{move-l} first, </td>

        <td id="L792" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="792"></td>
        <td id="LC792" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">of the structural congruence rules in Figure <span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">fig:sc</span>}. </td>

        <td id="LC823" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{<span class="pl-en">Base Excision Repair</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L824" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="824"></td>
        <td id="LC824" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-k">\label</span>{<span class="pl-v">sec:ber</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L825" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="825"></td>
        <td id="LC825" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L826" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="826"></td>
        <td id="LC826" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{<span class="pl-en">Description of Base Excision Repair</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L827" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="827"></td>
        <td id="LC827" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L828" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="828"></td>
        <td id="LC828" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This is from my thesis</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L829" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="829"></td>
        <td id="LC829" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L830" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="830"></td>
        <td id="LC830" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">So far we have seen some applications of CCB, which are very close to the original inspiration of the calculus. If the principles behind CCB are of some general relevance, there should be other processes we can model using our calculus. A candidate for these might be biological processes. These are ultimately chemical reactions, but they are often viewed at a much higher level of abstraction then we have done so far. Typically, in such studies atoms would no longer play a r\^{o}le, but proteins and other macromolecules, consisting of thousands or more atoms are considered as entities. Typical examples are pathways, gene regulation, transcription, or DNA repair. One of the mechanisms for DNA repair is \emph{base excision repair} (BER). Specifically, BER is responsible for repairing small damages, where a single base pair in the DNA is not correct. Such damages can be inflicted by processes in the body or various external factors like radiation. Repair of such damages is important to prevent a degradation of the DNA information in the organism. There are various subtypes of BER, and various proteins involved in it. For our purposes, we look at the case that a uracil base has been incorporated in the DNA. Uracil is normally only found in RNA, whereas DNA consists of the four bases adenine (A), cytosine (C), guanine (G), and thymine (T).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L831" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="831"></td>
        <td id="LC831" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L832" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="832"></td>
        <td id="LC832" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Uracil-DNA glycosylase (UNG or UDG) is the protein responsible for removing uracil from DNA and making the position available for insertion of the correct base. The process has been extensively studied\footnote{A good overview is given in \cite{pmid25252105}. We use a highly simplified view here. For example, there is not a single UDG, but a family of UDGs all exhibiting slightly different behaviour.} and modelled in \cite{Koehler2014} and \cite{kappadna}. A description of the process on an abstract level is as follows: UDG can bind to any of the deoxyribose/phosphate groups forming the backbone strands of the DNA. From there it can ``walk&#39;&#39; along the chain to the next deoxyribose/phosphate group (that walk makes it much more likely to find a damage than if UDG would just randomly bind to and get off the DNA strand again). If the base attached to this group is uracil, UDG will bind to it and dissolve the bond from the uracil to the DNA. Uracil can then be released and UDG can either continue the search or get off the DNA strand. The correct base can take the place of the uracil.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L833" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="833"></td>
        <td id="LC833" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L834" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="834"></td>
        <td id="LC834" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{<span class="pl-en">Modelling BER</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L835" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="835"></td>
        <td id="LC835" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L836" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="836"></td>
        <td id="LC836" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In order to model BER, we need the following components: deoxyribose/phosphate groups, the UDG, the uracil and the four other bases. The other bases will not take part in the reactions, but include them in our model in order to demonstrate the interaction we. The components are the following:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L837" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="837"></td>
        <td id="LC837" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L838" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="838"></td>
        <td id="LC838" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{array}{lll}</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L839" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="839"></td>
        <td id="LC839" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s">DP &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\bydef</span> &amp; (p<span class="pl-c1">3</span>,p<span class="pl-c1">5</span>,b,d).DP&#39;<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L840" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="840"></td>
        <td id="LC840" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s">UDG &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\bydef</span> &amp; (h;f).(e).UDG&#39;<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L841" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="841"></td>
        <td id="LC841" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s">U &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\bydef</span> &amp; (b;e).(u).U&#39;<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L842" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="842"></td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L843" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="843"></td>
        <td id="LC843" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s">T &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\bydef</span> &amp; (b;i).(t).T&#39;<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L844" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="844"></td>
        <td id="LC844" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s">G &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\bydef</span> &amp; (b;i).(g).G&#39;<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L845" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="845"></td>
        <td id="LC845" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s">C &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\bydef</span> &amp; (b;i).(c).C&#39;<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L846" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="846"></td>
        <td id="LC846" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{array}<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L847" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="847"></td>
        <td id="LC847" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L848" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="848"></td>
        <td id="LC848" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where processes <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> model the bases adenine (A), cytosine (C), guanine (G), thymine (T), and uracil (U) respectively. Process <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>UDG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> represents the Uracil-DNA glycosylase and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> a deoxyribose/phosphate group. Here <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>e<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are weak actions, all other actions, namely <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-c1">5</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>h<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are strong.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>

        <td id="L881" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="881"></td>
        <td id="LC881" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-c1">\caption</span>[A <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>UDG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> unit whilst performing a step along a DNA strand.]{A <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>UDG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> unit whilst performing a step along a DNA strand. The <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>hd<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> bond is broken together with the new <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>fd<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> being formed.}</td>

        <td id="LC882" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-k">\label</span>{<span class="pl-v">fig:berintermediate</span>}</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L883" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="883"></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L884" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="884"></td>
        <td id="LC884" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L885" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="885"></td>
        <td id="LC885" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We model the deoxyribose/phosphate groups first. This has two ends, normally called 3&#39; and 5&#39;, which we model as $p3$ and $p5$ actions respectively. They help us to build the DNA strands. Also, there is a $b$ action, which enables binding of a base. Then we need a possibility for the UDG to bind and to ``walk&#39;&#39;: this is enabled by actions $d$, $h$, and $f$, as we will see. UDG is modelled to have the prefix $(h;f)$, which enables the walk, since the strong action $h$ can be bonded to a $DP$ and $f$ can interact with a neighbouring $DP$. This breaks the $hd$ bond, and the $fd$ bond is then promoted to $d$, which gives us the $UDG$ being bonded to the neighbouring $DP$ the same way it was bound before to the other $DP$. Figure~\ref{fig:berintermediate} shows this intermediate situation whilst this step is performed. The five bases ($C$, $G$, $T$, $A$) all have a $b$ action to bind to a $DP$. If $A-T$ respectively $C-G$ are opposite each other they can bind and therefore form a correct base pair in the DNA. Uracil ($U$) is not able to form a base pair in our DNA context. All bases have a weak action in the prefix $(b;x)$. This action $x$ serves for removing the base from the DNA by breaking the $b$ bond. For uracil the action $x$ is $e$, for other bases it is $i$. By this UDG can be specific to uracil. In our model no action interacts with $i$, but of course other proteins not modelled might react with it. Note that $i$ and $e$ actions in the $U$, $A$, $T$, $G$, and $C$ processes cannot happen if the $u, a, t, g$ respctively $c$ actions are done, so $i$ and $e$ are blocked by $u, a, t, g,$ and $c$. Since $u, a, t, g$ and $c$ are used to form the base pairs this means that a correct base pair cannot be removed from the DNA in any case. This models the situation we need for the repair mechanism to work. We have used concerted actions in two instances here: Firstly to enable the UDG walk. This is an instance where backtracking would not work, since we need out-of-causal-order reversibility in this case. We cannot unbond from the old DP first and then choose the next $DP$, but we must hold the old bond until the new bond is formed. Secondly, we use a concerted action to enable the repair mechanism by making a bonding on the repair action break the bond to DP.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L886" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="886"></td>
        <td id="LC886" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L887" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="887"></td>
        <td id="LC887" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In the synchronisation function, we have the interaction of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-c1">5</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to form the strands, the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> interaction for binding the bases, the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>h<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> interaction for the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">``</span>walk<span class="pl-pds">&#39;&#39;</span></span>, the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> interactions for forming the base pairs, and the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>e<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>e<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> interaction for the repair action.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L888" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="888"></td>
        <td id="LC888" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L889" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="889"></td>
        <td id="LC889" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In order to model a strand of DNA, we restrict ourselves to three base pairs. This means we need six <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> processes and six bases. We put two <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">``</span>correct<span class="pl-pds">&#39;&#39;</span></span> base pairs and one containing a uracil base. An extra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> base must be available for replacing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. We also use subscripts to distinguish processes where there is more than one instance of the process. The system is modelled in CCB as follows:</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L890" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="890"></td>

        <td id="LC891" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{array}{l}</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L892" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="892"></td>
        <td id="LC892" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s">(DP_<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> DP_<span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> DP_<span class="pl-c1">3</span> <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> A <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> T <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> G_<span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> U <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> C_<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> C_<span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> DP_<span class="pl-c1">4</span> <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> DP_<span class="pl-c1">5</span> <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> DP_<span class="pl-c1">6</span> <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> UDG) <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L893" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="893"></td>
        <td id="LC893" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\setminus</span><span class="pl-c1">\{</span>p<span class="pl-c1">3</span>, p<span class="pl-c1">5</span>, d, b, a, t, g, e, u, c, h, f, i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span> </span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L894" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="894"></td>
        <td id="LC894" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{array}<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L895" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="895"></td>

        <td id="L927" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="927"></td>
        <td id="LC927" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Initially <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>UDG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> bonds to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, which in turn is bonded to a correct base pair (note <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>UDG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> was not bound so far to any other process). The situation is shown in Figure~<span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">fig:ber</span>} and is as follows (the bonds created, news keys and action on which keys were removed are shown in <span class="pl-c1">\textbf</span>{<span class="pl-mb">bold</span>}):</td>
      </tr>

      </tr>

        <td id="L930" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="930"></td>
        <td id="LC930" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;<span class="pl-c1">\xrightarrow</span>{hd[2]}(p3_1,p5_1[1],d_1<span class="pl-c1">\boldsymbol</span>{[2]},b_1[5]).DP_1&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> (p3_2[1],p5_2[3],d_2,b_2[4]).DP_2&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> &amp;&amp;<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L937" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="937"></td>
        <td id="LC937" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L938" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="938"></td>
        <td id="LC938" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The UDG can now randomly <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">``</span>walk<span class="pl-pds">&#39;&#39;</span></span> along the chain. The <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(h;f)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> prefix can appropriately model this, since if the weak <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> action binds to the neighbour, the bond on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>h<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is broken. In our case, action <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>UDG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> can communicate with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. This breaks bond 2 from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>h<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>UDG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, thus having performed a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">``</span>step<span class="pl-pds">&#39;&#39;</span></span>. We then move key <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">14</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>h<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (via the <span class="pl-c1">\rulename</span>{prom} rule from Figure~<span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">fig:reduction</span>}) and get:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L939" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="939"></td>

        <td id="LC941" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;<span class="pl-c1">\xrightarrow</span>{<span class="pl-cce">\{</span>fd[14],<span class="pl-c1">\underline</span>{hd}[2]<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\Rightarrow</span> (p3_1,p5_1[1],<span class="pl-c1">\boldsymbol</span>{d_1},b_1[5]).DP_1&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> (p3_2[1],p5_2[3],<span class="pl-c1">\boldsymbol</span>{d_2[14]},b_2[4]).DP_2&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span>&amp;&amp;<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>

        <td id="L942" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="942"></td>
        <td id="LC942" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;(p3_3[3],p5_3,d_3,b_3[9]).DP_3&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> (b_1[5];i_1).(a[6]).A&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> (b_2[7];i_2).(t[6]).T&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> (b_3[8];i_3).(g_1).G_1&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span>&amp;&amp;<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>

        <td id="LC943" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;((b_4[9];i_4).(g_2[10]).G_2&#39;  <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> (b_5[4];e_2).(u).U&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> (b_6[11];i_6).(c_1[10]).C&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> (b_7;i_7).(c_2).C&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span>&amp;&amp;<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L944" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="944"></td>
        <td id="LC944" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;(p3_4,p5_4[12],d_4,b_4[7]).DP_4&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> (p3_5[12],p5_5[13],d_5,b_5[8]).DP_5&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span><span class="pl-c1">\\</span> &amp;(p3_6[13],p5_6,d_6,b_6[11]).DP_6&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\paral</span> <span class="pl-c1">\boldsymbol</span>{(h[14];f)}.(e_2).UDG&#39;&amp;&amp;</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L945" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="945"></td>
        <td id="LC945" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{<span class="pl-smi">flalign*</span>}</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L946" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="946"></td>
        <td id="LC946" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L947" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="947"></td>
        <td id="LC947" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>UDG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> could now simply continue its walk, or it can interact via its <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>e<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> action with the uracil. Note that other bases expose the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> action, so uracil cannot interact with them. The <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, or <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span> c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> actions block <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>e<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> or <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, so correct base pairs are not affected by repairs. In our example <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>e_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>UDG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> interacts with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>e_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, breaking bond 4 between <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b_<span class="pl-c1">5</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>UDG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. We have achieved the desired repair, since the uracil is removed from the DNA. We model this by the following transition (we use the rewrite rule again):</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L989" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="989"></td>
        <td id="LC989" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L990" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="990"></td>
        <td id="LC990" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">If uracil would have been bonded on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, the interaction with UDG could not have happened, so the defect is recognized. We now have the uracil broken from the deoxyribose/phosphate group and the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> action on the deoxyribose/phosphate group ready to bond to another base. UDG needs to release <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and then either to continue its walk or release itself from the DNA. We can again use our new operator for modelling UDG, since this way we achieve that the repair mechanism happens. On the other hand by combining two groups of actions we <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">``</span>block<span class="pl-pds">&#39;&#39;</span></span> this repair to happen if the desired second bond is there.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L991" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="991"></td>
        <td id="LC991" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L992" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="992"></td>
        <td id="LC992" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A limitation of our modelling is that it allows the UDG during its <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">``</span>walk<span class="pl-pds">&#39;&#39;</span></span> to bind to any DG group, since there is no restriction which <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> action is used. In reality of course UDG must continue with the nearest DP group. This is a spatial effect our calculus does not model so far. Similarly, the repair by UDG binding to the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>e<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> action of a uracil (U) is not dependent on the UDG being next to it, whereas in reality it is. Again this is a spatial effect, which we will discuss in Section~<span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">sec:ccbs</span>}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L993" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="993"></td>
        <td id="LC993" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L994" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="994"></td>
        <td id="LC994" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We have used the software from Chapter~<span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">sec:simulation</span>} to test the modelling. The desired path is one of the possibilities, which shows that our modelling is adequate in this respect. We also get some undesired reactions: Apart from UDG binding to any DP group during its walk, there is also the possibility that the unused <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-c1">5</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> action of a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, which is at the end of the DNA strand, interacts with an unused <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> from the a DP at the other end of the DNA strand. This is not impossible as a such, but prevented in reality by at least two effects we do not model. One is again the spatial arrangement, the other is the fact that the ends of the DNA are protected by special groups, which we do not model here. They prevent reactions at the DNA ends.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L995" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="995"></td>
        <td id="LC995" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L996" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="996"></td>
        <td id="LC996" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{<span class="pl-en">DNA Mismatch Repair</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L997" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="997"></td>
        <td id="LC997" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-k">\label</span>{<span class="pl-v">sec:dnamimatch</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L998" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="998"></td>
        <td id="LC998" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L999" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="999"></td>
        <td id="LC999" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{<span class="pl-en">Description of DNA Mismatch Repair</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1000" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1000"></td>
        <td id="LC1000" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1001" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1001"></td>
        <td id="LC1001" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In Section~<span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">sec:ber</span>}, the problem was the incorporation into DNA of a base which should not occur in DNA at all. The repair relied on recognizing this base. Another possible error is that two bases are included which are both possible in DNA, but do not match, for example, a pair of adenine and cytosine. This can happen if, after the splitting of the double strand, the new strand intended to match the old one, does not actually match the old strand - for example, incorporating an adenine opposite a cytosine, which should normally be matched by a thymine.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1002" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1002"></td>
        <td id="LC1002" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1003" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1003"></td>
        <td id="LC1003" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Such a repair (a DNA mismatch repair) is not possible in the same way as the base excision repair, since any of the two bases could be wrong, so the non-matching  bases do not tell what to do. As before, we model the DNA mismatch repair process using several abstractions. A description of the process on an abstract level is as follows: If two bases are incorporated into a DNA strand which do not match (i.e. are not C/G or A/T pairs), this constitutes a defect in the DNA strand. A repair similar to BER is not possible, since it is not clear which of the two bases is correct just from the bases alone - both could be right. We are looking at a specific way to handle this situation, called Methyl Mismatch Repair (MMR). This is the repair mechanism in bacteria, in particular E. coli, for which detailed studies has been done.\footnote{Paul L. Modrich, Tomas Lindahl and Aziz Sancar received the Nobel Price in Chemistry 2015 for their work on DNA repair. Modrich&#39;s Nobel Lecture about Methyl-directed Mismatch Repair in E. coli and humans \cite{pmid27198632} gives a nice overview.} This process is based on DNA strands being methylated sometime after their creation. Methylation means the attachment a methyl group (a carbon atom with three hydrogen atoms), in this case to the Adenine base. Specifically, this happens whenever there is a GATC sequence. Since the methylation (which is done by specific proteins, which we do not model) happens with a delay after the duplication of a strand, for some time the old strand is methylated, the new strand is not. This enables the removal of exactly the new base, which must be the wrong one.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1004" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1004"></td>
        <td id="LC1004" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1005" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1005"></td>
        <td id="LC1005" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The actual repair involves the proteins MutS, MutL, MutH, and UvrD. MutS first binds to the mismatch and then recruits MutL and MutH. MutL can detected the methylated strand and can form a loop in the DNA. In this loop, the newer strand now is outside, whereas the old strand is covered by itself and MutL. MutH cleaves the unmethylated strand. This happens in some distance from the mismatch, due to the size of the proteins and the loop in the DNA. UvrD can then detect the cleavage and can move along the strand. It removes the outer strand when moving along. At the same time, the MutL, MutH, and MutS proteins are released and the loop in the DNA disappears. UvrD moves to after the mismatch, removing the wrong base together with their neighbours. UvrD then goes off the DNA and leaves the old, and correct, strand to be completed. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1006" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1006"></td>
        <td id="LC1006" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1007" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1007"></td>
        <td id="LC1007" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{<span class="pl-en">Modelling DNA Mismatch Repair</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1008" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1008"></td>
        <td id="LC1008" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1009" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1009"></td>
        <td id="LC1009" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For modelling MMR, we use the components from Section~<span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">sec:ber</span>} as much as possible. We reuse the deoxyribose/phosphate groups, and the four bases A, T, C, and G. We will extend those components where needed, but we will keep the original actions. Overall, in order to model MMR, we need the following components: deoxyribose/phosphate groups, the four bases A, T, G, C, the methyl group Me, and the proteins MutS, MutL, MutH, and UvrD. The reused components are the following:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1010" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1010"></td>
        <td id="LC1010" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>

        <td id="L1011" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1011"></td>

        <td id="L1012" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1012"></td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1013" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1013"></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L1014" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1014"></td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1017" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1017"></td>
        <td id="LC1017" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{array}<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1018" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1018"></td>
        <td id="LC1018" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1019" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1019"></td>
        <td id="LC1019" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where processes <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> model the bases adenine (A), cytosine (C), guanine (G), and thymine (T). Notice we have added actions <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>m<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>m<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is enabling the methylation. It only exists in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, since the methylation is only happending there. Also, the actions on DP have been regrouped (but all original actions are still there). In <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, we are now using a parallel operator. This is necessary to enable a breaking of a bond to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> or <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-c1">5</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> whilst there is still a bond to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. The action <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, which was used by UDG in the modelling of BER is not used here, as we will see. We keep it to have an extension of the previous modelling.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1020" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1020"></td>
        <td id="LC1020" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1021" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1021"></td>
        <td id="LC1021" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We also need additional components, namely the methyl group, the MutS, MutL, MutH, and UvrD proteins. We model these as follows:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1022" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1022"></td>
        <td id="LC1022" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{array}{lll}</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1023" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1023"></td>
        <td id="LC1023" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s">Me &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\bydef</span> &amp; (m).(n).Me&#39;<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></span></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L1025" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1025"></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L1027" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1027"></td>

        <td id="L1028" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1028"></td>
        <td id="LC1028" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{array}<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1029" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1029"></td>
        <td id="LC1029" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1030" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1030"></td>
        <td id="LC1030" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where processes <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>MutS<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>MutL<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>MutH<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>UvrD<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> model the MutS, MutL, MutH, and UvrD protein respectively.  Here <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are weak actions, all other actions, namely <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-c1">5</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>m<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>m<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>l<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>o<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>v<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>w<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, are strong. Notice that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is not used, but we keep it to have this model as an extension of the BER model. In <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>UvrD<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, we again use a  parallel operator. This will make it possible for UvrD to break two bonds with every <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">``</span>step<span class="pl-pds">&#39;&#39;</span></span> it moves.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1031" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1031"></td>
        <td id="LC1031" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1032" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1032"></td>
        <td id="LC1032" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1033" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1033"></td>
        <td id="LC1033" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The synchronisation function for our system is as follows:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1034" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1034"></td>

        <td id="LC1035" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\arraycolsep</span>=3.4pt<span class="pl-c1">\def\arraystretch</span>{1.0}</span></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L1037" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1037"></td>
        <td id="LC1037" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(p3,p5) &amp; = &amp; p &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(b,b) &amp; = &amp; bb &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(a,t) &amp; = &amp; at &amp;  <span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(g,c) &amp; = &amp; gc \\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1038" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1038"></td>
        <td id="LC1038" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\hline</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1039" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1039"></td>
        <td id="LC1039" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(m,m) &amp; = &amp; mm &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(m2,a) &amp; = &amp; m2a &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(m2, g) &amp; = &amp; m2g &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(m2,c) &amp; = &amp; m2c \\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1040" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1040"></td>
        <td id="LC1040" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\hline</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1041" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1041"></td>
        <td id="LC1041" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(m2,t) &amp; = &amp; m2t &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(l,l) &amp; = &amp; ll &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(n,n) &amp; = &amp; nn &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(o,o) &amp; = &amp; oo\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1042" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1042"></td>
        <td id="LC1042" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\hline</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1043" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1043"></td>
        <td id="LC1043" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(r,r) &amp; = &amp; rr &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(t,u) &amp; = &amp; tu &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(p,s) &amp; = &amp; ps &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(w,s) &amp; = &amp; ws\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1044" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1044"></td>
        <td id="LC1044" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\hline</span></span></td>

        <td id="L1045" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1045"></td>
        <td id="LC1045" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(v,p3) &amp; = &amp; vp3 &amp;  <span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(u,r) &amp; = &amp; ur  &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(s,v) &amp; = &amp; sv &amp; &amp; &amp; \\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1046" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1046"></td>
        <td id="LC1046" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{<span class="pl-smi">array</span>}</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1047" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1047"></td>
        <td id="LC1047" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">\]</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1048" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1048"></td>
        <td id="LC1048" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1049" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1049"></td>
        <td id="LC1049" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">As before, the deoxyribose/phosphate groups and the bases can combine to form a DNA strand. In that strand, there can be DNA mismatches. Note that we do not model how they happen, we just assume a DNA strand as in Figure~<span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">fig:state1</span>} with a DNA mismatch and correct pairs otherwise. The mismatch here is an A-G pair, but that is not crucial for our modelling. The A-G bases cannot bond to each other, that is the case in our modelling as well in reality, and this gives the opportunity for the repair. To the left of the DNA strand, there is a CTAG sequence (respectively a GATC sequence). This is where the methylation happens. In our case, we have a recently duplicated strand, where the older part is the upper one (A is methylated) and the newer part is the lower one (A is not methylated). The methylation itself is done by proteins which are not modelled here. This is the situation where the MMR can happen.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1050" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1050"></td>
        <td id="LC1050" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">

      </tr>

</td>
