      <tr>
        <td id="L1102" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1102"></td>
        <td id="LC1102" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In this short DNA section , we firstly have a mismatch - <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> do not form an A/T or G/C pair as required. Secondly, methylation has happened on the old half of the strand, which means that an methyl group (<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Me<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) is attached to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. Note that there is no methyl group on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. This is because the methylation only happens on CTAG sequences. This happens via a specific protein, which we do not model, we just assume the end result. No <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>s would be methylated on the new half, even if they were in a CTAG sequence, since not enough time has passed for this to happen.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1103" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1103"></td>
        <td id="LC1103" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1104" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1104"></td>
        <td id="LC1104" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">MutS can now bond to the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> bases,  specifically to processes <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>  via the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g_<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> actions. This is the recognition of the mismatch. Not that the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> actions are not available on matching pairs. So the bonding is not possible if the bases are properly paired, and also not if a Uracil is incorporated into the strand (as in the BER example). The transitions for creating the two bonds between <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>MutS<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L1207" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1207"></td>
        <td id="LC1207" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Note that execution of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s_<span class="pl-c1">9</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP_<span class="pl-c1">9</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> leads to breaking a bond between two deoxyribose/phosphate groups. Specifically, bond 33 from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>MutH<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP_<span class="pl-c1">9</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> via actions <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>w<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is formed and bond 13 between <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-c1">5</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP_<span class="pl-c1">8</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in  <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP_<span class="pl-c1">9</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is broken. We use a concerted action and rewriting for this. The situation after this step is shown in Figure~<span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">fig:state2</span>}. This has now the right DNA strand cleaved.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC1271" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    <span class="pl-c1">\includegraphics</span>[width=1.0<span class="pl-c1">\textwidth</span>]{mmr/state3}</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L1272" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1272"></td>
        <td id="LC1272" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-c1">\caption</span>[A six base pair DNA fragment.]{A six base pair DNA fragment, with a DNA mismatch and methylation of one strand. UvrD has now bonded to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP_{10}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, breaking the bonds of those molecules to the rest of the DNA via concerted actions (shown as dotted lines). In a next step, UvrD can now <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">``</span>walk<span class="pl-pds">&#39;&#39;</span></span> along the DNA strand, and remove the next pair.}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1273" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1273"></td>
        <td id="LC1273" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-k">\label</span>{<span class="pl-v">fig:state3</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1274" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1274"></td>
        <td id="LC1274" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{<span class="pl-smi">figure</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1275" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1275"></td>
        <td id="LC1275" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1276" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1276"></td>
        <td id="LC1276" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">From here, UvrD can <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">``</span>walk<span class="pl-pds">&#39;&#39;</span></span> along the strand. As opposed to BER, the bonds between the base pairs are now broken during the walk. In parallel, the bonds between the deoxyribose/phosphate groups are also broken as UvrD progresses. We write this as two separate concerted transitions here for clarity:</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC1317" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This is shown in Figure~<span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">fig:state4</span>}. Here, the first  base and deoxyribose/phosphate group has been removed (no longer shown in Figure~<span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">fig:state4</span>}) and UvrD is moving to the next  base and deoxyribose/phosphate group, again removing them.         <td id="LC1338" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    <span class="pl-c1">\includegraphics</span>[width=1.0<span class="pl-c1">\textwidth</span>]{mmr/state4}</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L1339" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1339"></td>
        <td id="LC1339" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-c1">\caption</span>[A six base pair DNA fragment.]{A six base pair DNA fragment, with a DNA mismatch and methylation of one strand. UvrD has now bonded to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>DP_{10}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, breaking the bonds of those molecules to the rest of the DNA via concerted actions (shown as dotted lines). This process can conitine for more pairs.}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1340" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1340"></td>
        <td id="LC1340" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-k">\label</span>{<span class="pl-v">fig:state4</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1341" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1341"></td>
        <td id="LC1341" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{<span class="pl-smi">figure</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1342" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1342"></td>
        <td id="LC1342" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1343" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1343"></td>
        <td id="LC1343" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This process can continue until the offending base has been removed. Figure~<span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">fig:state6</span>} shows the removal of the offending base. We do not model how the number of base pairs to remove is determined. In reality, that number is not fixed, but is determined by the interal workings of the protein, where the number is statistically distributed. Once this is done and the MutH, MutL, and MutS proteins have detached we get the situation shown in Figure~<span class="pl-k">\ref</span>{<span class="pl-c1">fig:state7</span>}. This is now ready for other proteins to replace the bases and and deoxyribose/phosphate groups. Notice that the remaining strand contains the necessary information for this, in particular only a T base can be put in opposite the A base. Note that the methyl group stays attached to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, since it is still an old DNA strand. Also the appropriate groups in the new, lower half will be methylated, so that both strands are marked as old material after the next DNA duplication process.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1344" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1344"></td>
        <td id="LC1344" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1345" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1345"></td>
        <td id="LC1345" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The modelling done so far does not involve any spatial configurataions. As in the BER example, this means that UvrD could bond to any deoxyribose/phosphate group, not just the neighbouring one. It also means that we have not modelled the formation of the loop in the DNA, which is crucial for cleaving the correct strand.</td>
      </tr>
